  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fe5cfaf2-8baf-464d-a4bf-7892899ae014'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="review_1113142728" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113142728" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31339793-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406624675p2/31339793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1113142728?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/31339793-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=laugh-out-loud">laugh-out-loud</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=book-comatose">book-comatose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=i-love-me-some-angst-drama">i-love-me-some-angst-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=buddy-recs">buddy-recs</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=swoon-worthy-guys">swoon-worthy-guys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1113142728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5183460712541613719"><b>5+ SHADOWHUNTER SERIES STARS! ★★★★★</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415524932i/11805548.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“We are all the pieces of what we remember. We hold in ourselves the hopes and fears of those who love us. As long as there is love and memory, there is no true loss.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><i>Oh. My. Gawd.</i> It's been almost 2 weeks since I read the last book in this series and at that point, I was left cuddling on my bed till my parents summoned me out of my room and saw me sniffling. Needless to say, I was beyond <i>wrecked</i> and felt like I was going through a 5-stage grief process thr</span>
  <span id="freeText5183460712541613719" style="display:none"><b>5+ SHADOWHUNTER SERIES STARS! ★★★★★</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415524932i/11805548.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“We are all the pieces of what we remember. We hold in ourselves the hopes and fears of those who love us. As long as there is love and memory, there is no true loss.”</i>
</b><br><br><i>Oh. My. Gawd.</i> It's been almost 2 weeks since I read the last book in this series and at that point, I was left cuddling on my bed till my parents summoned me out of my room and saw me sniffling. Needless to say, I was beyond <i>wrecked</i> and felt like I was going through a 5-stage grief process throughout this entire time. <br><br>I couldn't even bring myself to write a review back then because doing so felt like I was making a definite decision to say goodbye to my favorite Shadowhunters and frankly I'm still not ready to *sniffs*. <br><br><i>**This will be a consolidated review of the ENTIRE series.**</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414928498i/11705788.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Being an avid YA fantasy/dystopia reader back in 2012, I couldn't bring myself to pick up this series as it was still ongoing and wasn't sure if I wanted to invest my emotional being into such a long series. At that point, I was deeply invested into <i><u>The Hunger Games</u> trilogy</i> and wasn't ready to just move on yet. So even after watching City of Bones in cinemas and loving it, I still hesitated to pick it up. But as of recent after needing to shift out from my romance contemporary reads and with the added incentive from one of my trusted reading buddies, I decided to finally give this a go. <br><br><b>I'll just say that I have absolutely <i>zero</i> regrets of dedicating an entire week for this read. My only regret was probably not picking this up back in 2012.</b> <br><br>From Day 1 of CC week, I was immediately sucked into this Shadowhunter world and with the days in between, I felt like I was fighting alongside their battles and growing up with them. Up till the last day of me reading the final book, just as every character has fought till their very last drop of sweat, tears and blood; it was as overwhelming for me as for them too once we finally reach that finish line. <br><br><b>As a reader, I was no longer on the outside looking in; but somewhere along the way, I was a part of their world.</b> I grieved alongside them, I revelled in their victory. For every high and for every low moment, there was just so much to take away from them all. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415532672i/11806688.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Every single thing in this series <b>from the world-building to the character development and down to the plot details</b>; they were done so intricately with so many rich details woven in slowly along the way and ultimately led up to a more complex world that we first imagined. There were always twists that you won't see coming in every book and characters that will make you have a change of heart as they slowly weasel into it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415532741i/11806702.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Character development was definitely evident</b> throughout the series and the one thing that evoked so much powerful emotions in me as I read the final books were <b>how much these characters have come along since the very first one</b>. Gone were the reckless young teenage Shadowhunters and in came the mature, bolder version of these young warriors. <br><br>There will be moments of love and trust but also betrayal and heartbreak. <b>Moments that will make your heart flutter, moments that will shatter your heart beyond repair.</b> There was a point in the final book that left me sobbing uncontrollably as I watched it unravelled because I've grown so attached to these people. The emotions evoked were almost as real as it could possibly be. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415532741i/11806703.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending of the entire series may have not been the most ideal one, but in a way it was also <i>perfect.</i> It left an aching feel in my heart not just because it marked the end of the series and having to bid goodbye to my beloved Shadowhunters, but it was a <i>
  <b>good kind of ache</b>
</i> because after everything that these characters have endured throughout, they ended up in such a good place in the end. Ultimately, that's the best thing a reader could possibly ask for :')<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414928498i/11705788.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Overall this was truly an amazing series and one that everyone should attempt to read whether you're an avid reader of the fantasy genre.</b> After being immersed into the wizardy world back during my HP days, I never thought I would find another world like the Shadowhunter world to lose myself in. Honestly, it will be a long while before I can fully recover from this series but moving on, these characters will have a sure place in my heart now ♥♥. <br><br>Well it won't be too long till you see me picking up <i>The Infernal Devices trilogy</i> ;)<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5183460712541613719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1154833093" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1154833093" />
    <a title="Iain" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18231342-iain"><img alt="Iain" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362918496p2/18231342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1154833093?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iain" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iain" href="/user/show/18231342-iain">Iain</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18231342-iain?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1154833093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17923541480598683206">So here’s the thing. After reading the things that crop up on wordpress.com from time to time concerning Cassandra Clare and her notorious history as a “Big Name Fan” on the very permanent interwebz, I don’t have much respect for her as a writer. That being said, the trailer for The Mortal Instruments: City of Bones looks pretty good and I’m a huge sucker for young adult urban fantasy centered around female protagonists. Combine these factors with my good friend Lottie’s recent description of th</span>
  <span id="freeText17923541480598683206" style="display:none">So here’s the thing. After reading the things that crop up on wordpress.com from time to time concerning Cassandra Clare and her notorious history as a “Big Name Fan” on the very permanent interwebz, I don’t have much respect for her as a writer. That being said, the trailer for The Mortal Instruments: City of Bones looks pretty good and I’m a huge sucker for young adult urban fantasy centered around female protagonists. Combine these factors with my good friend Lottie’s recent description of the pseudo-incest plot in The Mortal Instruments, as well as her insistence that I’d love some of the queer characters in the novels (which was reiterated by my best friend), and I caved in spite of my dislike for the books’ author.<br /><br />In the last week, I’ve busted through all five books that have been published thus far in The Mortal Instruments series and made plans to read the series prequel, The Infernal Devices. I can say with conviction that I have never in my life been more torn about my feelings for a book series, most especially a fun and easy-to-read young adult series.<br /><br />The basic plot of The Mortal Instruments is that within the human world, there is another world that contains demons, greater demons, vampires, werewolves and other “downworlders” (known to Buffy fans as “baddies”), as well as shadowhunters. Shadowhunters were created when a mortal man drank the blood of an angel. (Or something. I’ve actually lost that thread somewhere along the way because I’ve been too busy tearing my hear out over the romantic drama in these books. That part is definitely riveting.) Shadowhunters are meant to protect humankind from demons and downworlders, which of course gets complicated. Enter some sycophants hellbent on destroying either the human world or the shadowhunter world (or both) and a girl named Clary Fray who was born a shadowhunter but never known life as anything other than a mundane (a “muggle,” for the Potterheads out there), and boom! You have a book series. As this book series progresses, you follow Clary and her friends as they fight evil and avoid death (some more successfully than others) and watch them all fall in love with each other.<br /><br />From a writer’s standpoint? The Mortal Instruments is a mess of overused metaphors and flowery language that’s too heavy even for the incredibly dramatic plot. Add in the fact that Clare has been accused of plagiarism and the writer side of me has to check out every time I open one of these books. From a reader’s standpoint? Well… that’s complicated. Clare has really interesting characters. I’m completely drawn to every single one of her major players, most especially the romantic and platonic ties between all of them. I constantly want to read more about the dramatic interplay between Clary and Jace, between Alec and Magnus, between Simon and Isabelle…<br /><br />Clare’s writing feels like fanfiction, which means that it’s incredibly easy and fast to read and that it keeps me interested, even when elements of it make me squirm or feel utterly ridiculous. I am so attached to her characters that I keep reading, despite the fact that overall, the books in this series are not that great. They aren’t worth the attachment. But the characters, as well as certain moments between the characters, make all of my irritation and frustration ultimately worth it. I have every intention of reading the sixth book in this series when it’s released, as well as the prequel series, The Infernal Devices. I have tweeted about and shouted about and updated people about my progress in the books, as well as my feelings throughout. I have gotten entirely too involved in this series, despite my lack of respect for Cassandra Clare, and I totally blame my friends for it. Will I be seeing the movie? Yes. Will I hate the casting? Most definitely. Will I see all of the movies after that? Probably.<br /><br />For now, I’m taking a break from this series (which in the fourth and fifth books has gotten way too cracky for my taste, but is still riveting enough to keep reading — you can read my individual reviews of the books on GoodReads [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]) to read other young adult books that I am also only interested in because of the upcoming film adaptations… But I know I’m going to get just as attached to the characters in The Infernal Devices. I have prepared myself for this downfall.<br /><br />I have developed a very love/hate relationship with The Mortal Instruments. I love the characters and the relationships. I hate the writing. I keep finding gaping holes in the plot. I can’t picture hardly anyone in the film cast properly filling the shoes of their roles (though my dream cast is quite lovely, I must say). I don’t respect Cassandra Clare or her writing. But I love Jace Wayland (Lightwood? spoiler alert!) and I love Alec Lightwood and I love Magnus Bane. I love Clary Fray. I love Isabelle Lightwood. I hate myself and my friends for convincing me to read this series.<br /><br />Remember when I said I was torn? I really, really meant it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17923541480598683206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1274340746" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1274340746" />
    <a title="Rants and Bants" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24862580-rants-and-bants"><img alt="Rants and Bants" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541473603p2/24862580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1274340746?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rants and Bants" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rants and Bants" href="/user/show/24862580-rants-and-bants">Rants and Bants</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=fairies">fairies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=collections">collections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=love-hate">love-hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1274340746&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1274340746" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6638131665765042105"><br/><br/><u>
  <b>Things The Series Did Right</b>
</u><br/><br/>-Worldbuilding<br/>-Descriptions<br/><br/>I could picture the characters and surroundings quite well. It all seemed very real to me, which is not always easy to do, but I rarely struggled with the writing and with imagining things in the books. Even during boring parts I would be able to read through it smoothly because the writing always flowed very well for me, and rarely left me confused or having to go back and re-read something. Sometimes certain parts even felt like how I m</span>
  <span id="freeText6638131665765042105" style="display:none"><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Things The Series Did Right</b>
</u><br /><br />-Worldbuilding<br />-Descriptions<br /><br />I could picture the characters and surroundings quite well. It all seemed very real to me, which is not always easy to do, but I rarely struggled with the writing and with imagining things in the books. Even during boring parts I would be able to read through it smoothly because the writing always flowed very well for me, and rarely left me confused or having to go back and re-read something. Sometimes certain parts even felt like how I myself would write something.<br /><br />-Side characters<br />-Side characters getting development/multiple POVs<br /><br />Some people don’t like the multiple POVs, but I personally do, just because it’s nice to get away from the main gang for a while. It also makes the story flow faster and more smoothly, for me anyway. HoN tries to do that, but fails miserably. Probably because I don’t care about ANY of the characters in that series, nor the plot or “writing” (if you can call it that). I think there were clear and distinct differences between the groups (Shadowhunters, the four Downworlder groups, mundanes, Silent Brothers, angels, demons, etc.) and I was able to get a sense of each of them. Obviously I wish that they’d focused on more than others, but that’s a different story.<br /><br />-Humor<br />-Building up suspense<br />-Lots of action and fight scenes. I liked how some of them were especially violent.<br />-Names. Yes, I liked quite a lot of the nomenclature in here.<br />-Diversity (It’s not required, but it is nice when a series has it)<br /><br />In fact, now that I think about it, pretty much all my favorite characters are nonwhite. Maia, Raphael, Magnus, Jem (I’m sure there are some dumbasses in the fandom who think those last two are white, even though it’s clearly stated that they’re not), and while I hate the term “whitewashing” for its overuse by abhorrent anti-white SJWs, I think it would probably be appropriate in the case of people wanting Magnus or Jem casted as white actors.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Things The Series Struggled Quite A Lot With</b>
</u><br /><br />-Having the characters always be likeable or sympathize-able.<br />-Forced relationships. Everybody is in a relationship. Everybody.<br />-Repeated descriptions<br />-Loose ends. <br /><br />The biggest one being that the Shadowhunters never learn from their bigotry. They, even some of the main characters, still think they’re better than Downworlders and mundanes, even after the sixth book. Which is really, really disappointing.<br /><br />-Inconsistencies with the characters.<br /><br />Something about these books that makes them so up –and-down for me is the fact that the characters just don’t seem consistent to me. Like let’s see—one minute, Alec is a raging asshole, the next, he’s this shy sensitive guy. I literally think he has two separate people living in him. That’s the only explanation. And Clary…the movie Clary and book Clary are COMPLETELY DIFFERENT PEOPLE. In the movie I felt so bad for how she was treated, she was nice to everyone and the Lightwoods preyed on her and ripped her to shreds, but in the books…in the books everybody loves her, almost immediately, and she is high-and-mighty as a result (though she’s like that anyway). It’s just super freaky. It’s almost like I can’t decide on a final opinion about these people, because they are so contradictory in themselves.<br /><br />-Double Standards<br /><br />I hate to be the bearer of bad news, but the following are a disturbing amount of double standards in these books that I’d like to point out:<br /><br />-Jocelyn makes ONE mistake (erasing her daughter’s memories to protect her) and she is set up on a cross and burned to death for it. Clary KEEPS making the SAME mistakes over and over and OVER again (being rash and impulsive, running off into danger, having no regard for who it affects whatsoever), yet is praised endlessly to the very end. The ONLY time somebody decides to call her out on her shit is when Luke scolds her for creating that stupid Portal in City of Glass, but then again, Luke is barely around after that, and we conveniently leave Clary being surrounded by all who love her.<br /><br />-Jocelyn makes that mistake and no one can forgive her. Alec makes the mistake of considering taking Magnus’s immortality away, and we have a whole army raiding down on Magnus to forgive Alec and get back together with him immediately. How DARE Magnus be a little hurt by someone’s betrayal and therefore want some time away from them???<br /><br />-Clary gets angry all the time, screams at people, and oftentimes gets violent. Yet we’re supposed to just accept this without complain, cuz you know, that’s Clary for ya! Jocelyn gets mad ONE time, justifiably, because her stupid selfish daughter goes running off and no one thought to tell Jocelyn this or even sympathize with her, after she went through the EFFORT to bring Clary somewhere safe, and we’re supposed to believe Jocelyn’s not allowed to get angry at all. She’s vilified for having the same human emotion that CLARY is always exhibiting.<br /><br />-Clary arrives in the City of Glass completely shocked and appalled that no one wants to see her, and it’s a big old pityfest when Jace yells at her (even though he was right about what he said), and poor Clary, poor poor wittle Clary…when Jocelyn arrives in the City of Glass to see her daughter, after committing the unthinkable act of WAKING UP FROM A COMA, Clary fucking screams at her and RAILROADS her into the next town! But Clary is still treated like the victim, even though she’s the one who abused her mother, and acted EXACTLY the same way she didn’t want someone else acting towards her earlier on.<br /><br />I mean goodness, there are enough double standards here to fill up a whole train station! It’s like unless you absolutely agree with every single thing the main group of characters are doing, and unless you absolutely love them, you’re just a bad person who deserves to be cast aside. No matter what they’re doing is stupid, and never mind how it may be affecting you…you don’t matter, they do, so you HAVE to agree with what they’re doing or else. I mean jeez…just because someone’s the main character doesn’t mean they’re perfect, always right, and exempt from criticism. A good writer knows this.<br /> <br />That’s why I’d started to have some faith in CoG when Luke, the closest anyone came in this entire series, actually called Clary out on her shit when she decided to go and create that stupid Portal, literally in the middle of Magnus and Luke yelling at her to stop it and explaining to her how it’s dangerous and why she shouldn’t do it. I would’ve thought Clary would’ve learned a huge lesson after that, that she would’ve grown and matured and developed as a character and been more thoughtful from that point forward when doing things. But no…she literally just keeps on doing the same thing over and over and OVER throughout the entire series, and people stop criticizing her and instead start praising her! She isn’t brave...she’s stupid. It’s as plain and simple as that. <br /><br />This series has the exact opposite problem of Eona. In that series, the main character is mistreated horribly and she’s actually a great person who deserved a lot more credit and respect. In this series…you freaking hate the main character, she’s so unlikeable, but she’s a total Mary Sue because everybody loves her, and the people that ever criticize are the vilified for it immediately. And what is with the ageism in this books? Honestly, I love YA, but it really feels like all the teen characters in here are treated like speshul little snowflakes just because they’re young, and ALL of the adult characters—with the exception of Magnus—are treated as insignificant, annoying, ignorant people that just need to be pushed aside. And Jocelyn and Luke’s love is treated as “disgusting” while Clary and Jace’s “I love you after only a few months and will sacrifice everything for you at the cost of hurting my mother” is supposed to be sweet???<br /><br />Also, Can I just say that some people would LOVE to have Jocelyn as a mother? I mean, ASIDE from not being allowed to watch anime/Disney movies (but then again, Clary probably did that at Simon’s house, or in secret, I mean how could Jocelyn actually know?), she actually let Clary have the freedom to socialize. When I was little, I wasn’t allowed to do ANYTHING. I wasn’t allowed to have friends come over, I wasn’t allowed to go to other friends’ houses, I wasn’t allowed to go out anywhere with them, even if there was adult supervision…hell I was barely allowed to talk on the phone or online. I wasn’t allowed to even trick-or-treat with my own friend who lived in the same neighborhood as me, I had to STRUGGLE just to do THAT for a LITTLE while. So to read about this little brat who got to have it all while she was growing up…it just pisses me the fuck off. And I don’t want ANYONE to try to tell me that Clary Fray was sheltered and treated like a prisoner and not allowed to have any freedom. Because if I’D walked out of the house to go somewhere with someone when I was her age, I’d have had the motherfucking cops called on me.<br /><br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>The Characters</b>
</u><br /><br /><b>Clary-</b> Okay in the first book, then became a bitch. She snaps at everybody. I don’t like people who snap.<br /><br /><b>Jace-</b> He goes back and forth between being funny to me, to being annoyingly boring, overdone, and the center of everything. I mean does he have to be loved by EVERYONE? The thing about the “bad boy” or the “anti-hero” or whatever is that they’re not supposed to be loved by the majority of the characters, and in fact, that’s what makes it so much more likely that the reader/viewer will like them. They’re not shoved down your throat. I thought he was pretty okay in the first three books, but the thing that just made me annoyed with him in the last three is that it still continued to be <i>all about him</i>—we have so many characters in here. Can’t we have the central plot focus on somebody else for a change? Like he is literally always at the center of everything—Valentine’s son, cursed, heavenly fire running through his veins, possessed—like wow. EVERYTHING happens to him. He never gets a break, does he? It’s just overkill to me. <br /><br /><b>Isabelle-</b> Okay in the first book, then became a bitch. She snaps at everybody and has a massive victim complex. <br /><br /><b>Alec-</b> He is really back-and-forth for me. Books 1, 5, and 6 he mostly annoyed me. Books 2 and 3 he was alright. I don’t really like how the fact that he’s gay and oppressed seems to be used as an excuse for his irrational anger towards people who haven’t done anything to him. I don’t tolerate those kind of people or that type of behavior. I am a very staunch believer in, “Judge a person on their character”, though I know that sadly many other people aren’t. Plus, you could easily argue that he’s also privileged in a way, since he’s a Shadowhunter, is part of a prestige family, has friends by his side all the time, and in the end, his father accepts him. And he’s got the delicious Magnus Bane in love with him, even after being whiny and difficult towards him.<br /><br />I also don’t like how he’s always defending Isabelle. It’s like she’s allowed to be a mean and rude to everybody as much as she wants, yet no one’s ever allowed to be remotely smart to her back. Or even when they’re being NICE to her he still gets mad for some reason…<br /><br /><b>Simon-</b> The only character who ends up changing for the better. In the first two books I did not like him because of the obnoxious , “I’m a nice guy and I’m being friendzoned” mentality. But once he dropped that, it was really nice. I don’t like how the ONLY reason the others seem to care about him after a while is because he’s a vampire and then potentially a Shadowhunter. They’re still stuck-up assholes towards mundanes, they still don’t really like Simon for Simon, they just like what he can do and provide for them. If he’d remained a mundane, they wouldn’t have given half a shit about him. And that makes me so mad. I mean it’s weird in a way, so many readers out there love Jace and Alec and Isabelle, but the truth is, they wouldn’t give two shits about you guys. At all. They really wouldn’t. Because you’re mundanes. I mean why would you like characters that you know for a fact would hate you if they were real???<br /><br /><b>Valentine and Sebastian—</b> Valentine was a pretty good villain, Sebastian…eh. The only things I found fascinating about him were that A) he literally fooled everyone for an entire book that he was someone else completely, from his name and identity down to his looks, which in retrospect makes them all look stupid. So kudos to him for that. And B) his final moments in Heavenly Fire as Jonathan Morgenstern. That was pretty epic right there. Didn’t know that was going to happen.<br /><br /><b>Helen and Aline-</b>Really wish there would’ve been more of them in here…they seemed a lot stronger and more likeable than our main heroines.<br /><br /><b>Jocelyn and Luke-</b>One of the best couples in here, but they’re sadly shoved aside a lot, because there’s this weird anti-older people stigma going on in the books. Like anyone who’s over their teens or twenties suddenly don’t matter anymore, are “disgusting” for being in love, and deserve ridicule. Meanwhile we’re subjected to having “Clace” and “Sizzy” shoved down our throats like they’re the most important things ever. Get me a bucket.<br /><br />I’ve already talked numerous times about how Jocelyn needs to do something about Clary’s attitude. If Clary were my child, I’d beat her. I’d beat her hard. There is literally not ONE book in this entire series where she is remotely respectful to her mother. Clary is so lucky I’m not her mother, or she’d be in for a whole different life.<br /><br />By the way, Jocelyn’s a painter, and I would’ve loved more details about that. I mean in all the detail they go in about Shadowhunting, fighting demons, killing things, etc…it would be nice if they could talk about somebody else’s hobbies for a change. Something that was actually peaceful and didn’t involve so much stress or violence. But then, maybe that’s because I started re-watching Bob Ross when I started doing this review.<br /><br /><b>Maia (The REAL heroine)—</b> Oh Maia….how I love you. You rock. Everything about you rocks. Stay you, keep doing you, don’t ever change. And truthfully speaking, you deserved Simon WAY more than Isabitch ever did.<br /><br /><b>Raphael and Magnus-</b> My two faves!!!! I look forward to reading The Bane Chronicles, especially as one of the stories has Raphael in it too! They are both so awesome, and I love how they don’t hold back from mocking the Shadowhunters. I love how they look out for their own interests. I admire their self-preservation, rather than being guilt-tripped by other people and their silly “morals”. It’s nice when characters have backbones, ya know?<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6638131665765042105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3551179461" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3551179461" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/114581082-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600965743p2/114581082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3551179461?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/114581082-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Capa comum 9789951115032" href="/book/show/28682622-the-mortal-instruments-the-complete-collection">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114581082-ari?shelf=female-writer">female-writer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114581082-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3551179461&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3551179461" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1011422180495604650">So it has been exactly two years since I read the first book and my opinion about TMI has changed A LOT. Here's my two cents:<br/>1. The Writing<br/> I love Cassandra Clare's books but I cannot stand her writing. It's flowery, over the top and way too dramatic. It doesn't exactly fit with the genre TMI is usually classified as,ie Urban Fantasy. The characters' descriptions are odd and it makes them feel a tad too inhuman. Reading her books put me in horrible reading slumps(but that's a me problem so I'm n</span>
  <span id="freeText1011422180495604650" style="display:none">So it has been exactly two years since I read the first book and my opinion about TMI has changed A LOT. Here's my two cents:<br />1. The Writing<br /> I love Cassandra Clare's books but I cannot stand her writing. It's flowery, over the top and way too dramatic. It doesn't exactly fit with the genre TMI is usually classified as,ie Urban Fantasy. The characters' descriptions are odd and it makes them feel a tad too inhuman. Reading her books put me in horrible reading slumps(but that's a me problem so I'm not really blaming her).<br />2. Characters<br />I feel like I'm the only one who doesn't really care about the characters. The characters I liked in the series are: Isabelle, Maia, Jordan, Alec, Simon and Magnus. Others were pretty meh. <br />I despise Clary but I have to admit she is a pretty realistic protagonist. She sucks at almost everything when she first starts training and I appreciate that. Apart from that I thought she was stupid and a bit of a damsel in distress. She is like a combination of Bella Swan, Anastasia Steele and regular old Mary Sue. So yeah not a fan.<br />3. The Relationships<br />Oh dear god the relationships. They are the aspect of the books I hate the most. Unnecessary and predictable love triangles, instalove, incest you name it, it's got it. I feel like a part of my heart has permanently frozen from the hate I have for Clace. Ugh. <br />4. Clace<br />Speaking of Clace, I detest them together. I don't even remember why at this point. Maybe the not-really-but-kinda incest. Or maybe it was the mind numbing back and forth that pissed me off. And Jace's general attitude towards everyone(Clary in particular) made me not want them together. The instalove was the worst aspect. <br />5. Overused and Poorly Executed tropes<br />Trope 1: Bad Boy With Tragic Past-Jace Herondale/Morgenstern/Wayland<br />This trope is so overused. Jace had a tragic past which allows him to be mean to basically everyone. Boohoo. I get that its a defense mechanism or whatever but its so overdone and badly written that I cannot look past it.<br />Trope 2: I'm Not Like Other Girls/Basic Mary Sue: Clary is boring and stereotypical. She doesn't recognise her self worth and beauty until she starts dating a guy. Yay... Clary is basically the blonde in horror movies who dies first(ie till the first 5 books, she does get better so props to her for that).<br />Trope 3: Nerdy Best Friend: Simon Lewis. He gets better though, most of the characters have pretty great character arcs.<br /><br />6. World Building and Magic Systems<br />I absolutely loved the world building and the magic system. I think this is what kept me reading despite everything. It was amazing. The concept was great, the execution was great too. The Downworlders were well written, I loved the way Shadowhunters were described.<br /><br />Now, tiny reviews of each books<br />1. City of Bones: 4 stars.<br />Notes: Fast paced, interesting, well written, great introduction to the Shadowhunters Universe.<br />2. City of Ashes: 3 stars.<br />Notes: Slow Paced, unnecessary, had fun drama, entertaining<br />3. City of Glass: 4.5 stars.<br />Notes: Loved it but Jace being revived almost ruined the entire series.<br />4. City of Fallen Angels: 3/2.75 stars<br />Notes: Could've been wrapped up in the third book,boring, liked the beginning, hated the end<br />5. City of Lost Souls:4.5 stars.<br />Notes: Loved Clary's character development, hated Jace, Sebastian was interesting but he was still kind of a dumb and random villian.<br />6. City of Heavenly Fire: 4.5 stars.<br />Notes:Good book, bad epilogue, wrapped things up a tad too neatly, Clace gets better<br /><br />thats it! Adios</span>
  <a data-text-id="1011422180495604650" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6758101506759907756" style="display:none">These books written by Cassie causes addiction to me! I started reading CoB last year and it was the first fantasy book that I've ever read. The sequels were not arrived in my country yet, so I waited and finally I've finished this book until CoHF! I went the adventures with Clary and Jace or in the other words, CLACE together with them. It was very fun and enjoyable spending my time with them. I love Simon the most! He has been a very good friend to Clary, which he finally gave his memories to Magnus's father just to save his friends. And of course, the tears were running down my cheeks accepting the fact that Simon could not remembered anything after a while. Isabelle Lightwood? In my eyes according to the book, she is a very beautiful, strong hearted and obviously brave. That's why I ship Simon and Isabelle so much! It looks like they are so meant to be. I have never liked gays partner before but since I met Magnus and Alec or MALEC, and now I love gays! (ignore my retardness) As for Jordan Kyle was one of my favorite boys in the book, I grief over his death. I can't stop my tears when he is dead, and Maia must have loved him so much. Luke? He is my favoritw too, I was imagining him being my father. He has been great to Clary and Jocelyn. Jocelyn? She has been a great mother of all, she even left the world of shadowhunters just to save Clary from Valentine. Through my POV, I never hated Sebastian &amp; Valentine much as I hate President Snow in THG. I love them as much as I love Simon, as they were doing all kinds of bad things on a shucking purpose. (don't judge me, i love every characters there) So have I mentioned all of them? Oh there's a lot of them actually. As for Jace &amp; Clary, after getting through their hard times, blamed as siblings by Valentine, they were strong back then. And finally the truth has revealed, I couldn't be much grateful. The love that was born in their hearts are very bound and strong. I love them so much!!!!!! Kbye that's for all. Read my next review on the other books!!!!! </span>

<div id="review_3585930545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3585930545" />
    <a title="Steff Pasciuti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10337759-steff-pasciuti"><img alt="Steff Pasciuti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600380747p2/10337759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3585930545?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steff Pasciuti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steff Pasciuti" href="/user/show/10337759-steff-pasciuti">Steff Pasciuti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3585930545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer330116623332357891">| <a href='https://spasciuti.com/review/city-of-bones-cassandra-clare/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reader Fox Blog</a> | <br/><a href='https://spasciuti.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586415338i/29258676.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>This was...a go back and reread before I get read of all the copies I own on account of the plagiarism. I’ve had these books for a long while, before I ever knew about those issues and, while I cannot fully remove myself from the stain that comes with having given this woman money, I can at least rid myself of the copies in the hopes that someone else will be spared that. Full review to come.<br/><br/><b>EDIT:</b> I've written a full review, though what is below has been heavily edited du</span>
  <span id="freeText330116623332357891" style="display:none">| <a href="https://spasciuti.com/review/city-of-bones-cassandra-clare/" rel="nofollow noopener">Reader Fox Blog</a> | <br><a href="https://spasciuti.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586415338i/29258676.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This was...a go back and reread before I get read of all the copies I own on account of the plagiarism. I’ve had these books for a long while, before I ever knew about those issues and, while I cannot fully remove myself from the stain that comes with having given this woman money, I can at least rid myself of the copies in the hopes that someone else will be spared that. Full review to come.<br><br><b>EDIT:</b> I've written a full review, though what is below has been heavily edited due to Goodreads' policies regarding commentary of author behavior within a review. In light of this, you can find the <a href="http://spasciuti.com/2019/04/18/city-of-bones-cassandra-clare/" rel="nofollow noopener">full review on my blog</a>. <br><br>My past with <i>City of Bones</i> is actually somewhat of an amusing one at times, but also a rather dejecting one. I cannot even begin with how devastated I was when I first learned of all the issues surrounding these novels and the author who penned them. The interesting thing is that I really enjoyed the books when I first came across them as a teenager, so much so that my first-ever rating of the book was five stars. As I've grown up I find myself feeling more and more embarrassed and disgusted with the fact that I bought these books. Just as I did with <i>Twilight</i> a few months ago, I've decided to re-read Clare's work before ridding myself of the books I've had since high school. I haven't decided yet whether to donate or throw them out, honestly, since I don't know if I want to subject other young readers to them but I definitely don't want these books anymore. And in this sense, I've decided to review each of her books. <br><br>As for <i>City of Bones</i>, the fact of the matter is that the novel is largely based around ideas that were borrowed and pulled from a variety of other novels and altered in various, somewhat minute ways in order for the work to transform into Clare's own piece of fiction. Looking below the surface of it all, though, it becomes difficult for me to credit much of the story and the characters to Clare's writing ability as a result of my understanding of where it all came from. I find myself unable to ascertain whether the bits about the story that I enjoyed were actually a result of Clare's own imagination or whether they were borrowed from somewhere else. You really don't have to look far at other reviews to see where the ideas for her story and characters come from, though the majority does appear to be based around Harry Potter.<br><br>Clare also has a rather annoying habit of creating extensive love polygons that just become absolutely ridiculous. I've drawn some out before, but just taking a look at this book alone you can see an extensive intermingling of love relationships/pinings. We'll begin with Clary, who can be romantically linked in this novel to both Jace and Simon. Jace can be linked to Clary and Alec. Simon can be linked to Clary and Isabelle. Alec can be linked to Jace and Magnus. Isabelle can be linked to Simon and Meliorn. And that, my friends, is just the first book. It'll get worse later on. Frankly, it's just far too much drama for it to all be necessary.<br><br>I can see, at times, why I enjoyed reading this story all those years ago. And I recall becoming emotionally invested enough for this to be the first book I actually threw against a wall upon finishing--I too was thoroughly upset and disgusted with the news brought to light for Clary and Jace via Valentine--and had I not already bought the whole series (I was a little excessive when buying books back then, as I'd not come across the concept that it's perfectly okay to begin a series and not continue on with it) I don't know if I'd have kept reading enough to find out the resolution to this exceedingly disturbing reveal. But I also loved <i>Twilight</i> at this point in my life, to the point that I wasn't aware enough of consent to find the actions of Jacob Black as disgusting as they truly are, so really, can I credit much to the fact that I liked this series? I'm not sure.<br><br>Where I'll occasionally find myself rather endeared toward characters, particularly <i>Simon</i>, other characters are frustrating and quick to anger, all of which often ultimately leads to incredibly poor decision making. And I'm left wondering how I liked any of these characters to begin with. There are a lot of problematic pieces to the book as a whole, some of which stem from the blatant ways in which Jace will lash out at anyone, anytime he feels like, others that lie within the unfortunate girl-hate dynamic that exists between Isabelle and Clary, and more that comes from the servant-like roles the gay characters in this novel hold or the power dynamics between an older man in a relationship with a <i>much</i> younger man. I could go on and on about this, but the truth is that others have as well. And you don't have to look far to find it all.<br><br>Clare's writing, overall, is inconsistent in quality which often leads me to wonder how much of what I really liked was not her work. While enough was altered for Clare to avoid a plagiarism lawsuit--fair enough--it still leaves me feeling deeply unsure, almost to the point that I hope the parts I like are not hers. Ultimately, though, even I have noticed many grammatical errors and typos throughout the novel. The degree of information that is simply thrown at us rather than shown is immense and often I find that characters don't always act in realistic manners. I'll give her this, though; <i>City of Bones</i> is infinitely better written than <i>Fifty Shades of Gray</i>, so at least she has that merit. All in all, while I was once quite a fan of these books, I'm not as much any longer. Even the show, which I do actually enjoy quite a lot and has fixed numerous issues that the books had, is somewhat seeped in the unfortunate disgrace of the material it is adapted from.<br><br>| <a href="https://www.instagram.com/spasciuti/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://mobile.twitter.com/SPasciuti_" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://spasciuti.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Reader Fox Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/@spasciuti" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a> | <a href="https://m.facebook.com/SteffPasciutiReaderFox/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> |</span>
  <a data-text-id="330116623332357891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11382252743509682560" style="display:none">Doing a review on the series all together. All in all I would give it 4 stars, but that’s only because the last 3 books saved it. The first three books were unnecessary and lowkey bad, Cassie should’ve just either made it two separate trilogy’s or kept the last 3. I will miss these characters, but I’m looking forward to reading TDA, maybe some characters will pop up in that?? Also the spines are gorgeous on my bookshelf. </span>

  <span id="freeText13867523539370380706" style="display:none">I had read TMI a while back and liked them but only remembered the bigger picture. And now that I’m on bookstagram I saw a lot of talk about them so I decided to read them again. <br /><br />I still like the series but I did struggle through the series. I also think now that I’m older I saw things/characters in another light. For example, I’m pretty sure that my first time I didn’t dislike Clary as much as I did this time around, she really annoyed me. I guess what bothered me was her foolishly threw herself and others in danger without thinking things through. And I’m all about saving your love and whatnot but at times the Jace/Clary relationship was over the top. <br /><br />Poor Simon…he really has it tough all around, I’m reading the Tales from Shadowhunter Academy, and it’s making happy to see him let his friends go to find himself. <br /><br />So many great characters are part of the series that end up dying and some of those just tore my heart apart!! <br /><br />With this re-read, I definitely have more details in mind and also made me want to read the other Shadowhunter universe books. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1391403747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10334936387740743007">Okay I know going into the Mortal Instruments series that it's going to be one of those guilty pleasure reads that you can't take too seriously. As a fan of Buffy the Vampire Slayer, it definitely kept me hooked on this new universe of supernatural creatures and the teenagers fighting them.<br/><br/>Books 1-3 were quite enjoyable and Cassandra Clare should've ended the series as a trilogy. Come time for books 4-6 and you know she is still cashing in. By this point, the other minor characters are pushed to</span>
  <span id="freeText10334936387740743007" style="display:none">Okay I know going into the Mortal Instruments series that it's going to be one of those guilty pleasure reads that you can't take too seriously. As a fan of Buffy the Vampire Slayer, it definitely kept me hooked on this new universe of supernatural creatures and the teenagers fighting them.<br /><br />Books 1-3 were quite enjoyable and Cassandra Clare should've ended the series as a trilogy. Come time for books 4-6 and you know she is still cashing in. By this point, the other minor characters are pushed to the forefront, which is fine, but with the ongoing shitstorm of soap opera relationships, I was starting to lose interest in this people.<br /><br />What happened here? Did we suddenly drop the ball and pull out every conceivable way to make the plot even remotely interesting. Apparently not. Sadly, I'll give this series and so-so grade. It didn't really inspire me to continue reading so I'll leave it up to the reader to decide if they like this series or not.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1349179832" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1349179832" />
    <a title="Ridan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24001287-ridan"><img alt="Ridan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391446939p2/24001287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1349179832?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ridan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ridan" href="/user/show/24001287-ridan">Ridan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1349179832&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1349179832" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7876183526680733279">Wow. So, I have a few things to say about this series of books; it's not perfect. There are many many flaws in Cassandra Clare's writing but you know what? SUCH an addictive series! I am OBSESSED with this!<br/><br/>So there are six books in this series, usually I would say that's a little too many but to be honest I think it kind of worked here.<br/><br/>I'll start off with the plot. The plot is all right, but the thing is with these books is that the plot was going on strong and sturdy up until book 3 (City Of Gl</span>
  <span id="freeText7876183526680733279" style="display:none">Wow. So, I have a few things to say about this series of books; it's not perfect. There are many many flaws in Cassandra Clare's writing but you know what? SUCH an addictive series! I am OBSESSED with this!<br /><br />So there are six books in this series, usually I would say that's a little too many but to be honest I think it kind of worked here.<br /><br />I'll start off with the plot. The plot is all right, but the thing is with these books is that the plot was going on strong and sturdy up until book 3 (City Of Glass), at the end of City of Glass everything had been tied up neatly and I was very happy with the ending. I think I remember even Cassandra Clare saying that she was originally supposed to only have three books in the series. But then suddenly City Of Fallen angels came along and I really did think it was the weakest book in the entire series. Hardly anything happened, Clary was just as annoying and selfish as ever, and it was just flimsy and didn't feel right. And then it was the same for City of Lost Souls, the only reason I enjoyed City Of Lost Souls was because Sebastian is my favourite character and there's LOADS of him in that book so I was basically thrilled.<br /><br />But I still think this should have ended at the third book. I loved City Of Heavenly Fire and I was pretty satisfied when this series ended... I just think City of Glass was just wrapped up way too well. I loved Sebastian as a character, he's my favourite and I'm glad the continuation of the series lead to a better exploration of his behaviour and objectives; I just think it should have remained as a trilogy because despite the introduction of the better characters - it still meant the less interesting characters such as Clary and Maia had to be dragged out even more which just got tedious after a while. <br /><br />I like to see this series as two parts, obviously the first three books follow one story line while the 4th, 5th, and 6th book follow another. It just seemed a bit higgledy piggledy and not very well organised. <br /><br />Another issue I had with this series, the same only issue I had with The Infernal Devices, was how Cassandra Clare likes to drift of to what the minor characters are doing. I honestly hate that. It was even worse in City of Heavenly Fire when Cassandra characters from the sequel series (The Dark Artifices) were introduced... and took up half the fucking book. I adored Mark Blackthorn. I cannot WAIT to read about him and I think he's the only reason I will carry on reading these. And Cassandra Clary has also very sneakily put him into the Shadowhunter Chronicles (a series of short stories) to so I guess I'll have to read them too.<br /><br />But I was pretty annoyed with the new characters taking up so much of the books. I don't give a shit about Emma- I don't know who she is and I don't want to know either. She seems like a brat. And I only sort of cared about Julian but I can all ready sense that he's just going to be another cocky love interested like Will and Jace. <br /><br />And I don't give a shit about Jordan and Maia, I really don't. I want to find out what's happening with Sebastian. Maia was honestly the least interesting character of the series. Her entire story was created around her miserably forced back story being constantly forced down our throats. And you know what I hate even more? How Cassandra Clare accused people who dislike Maia of being racist. No, it's not that I disliked Maia because she was black. I dislike Maia because she was uninteresting, stroppy and selfish. I found her just as annoying as Clary. And Clary is white. And another point; I liked Raphael and he was Mexican. I liked Jem and he was half Chinese. I liked Magnus and he's half Indonesian. No. I am not racist. I just have an opinion. <br /><br />And now with the characters. Clary is the most idiotic female protagonist I've ever read about. She settles right in nicely with Ever from the Immortals series and Bella from Twilight. These three are like the trio of idiots in YA literature. Oh my god, don't even get me started on how many times I wanted to slap Clary. Selfish bitch. Stupid bitch. She happily dances off into trouble like some naive little pansy. All she ever cares about is her and Jace. My god woman! Get. A. Grip. She's met Jace for like a month and suddenly he's the only thing she cares about. I don't really like to throw the Mary Sue word around but it just seemed necessary here. Sure, her stupidity may be a flaw, but the book doesn't portray it as a stupidity, it portrays it as a completely normal thing to do.<br /><br />There's a bit in City Of Ashes when they go to visit the Seelie Court for information off the Seelie Queen. Jace clearly explains to Clary 'Do not eat or drink anything the faeries give you', and they're all handed out drinks during the viewing. And guess what Clary does? 'Oooohhh, a drink, I think I'll just STICK MY FINGERS IN IT AND THEN SHOVE MY FINGERS IN MY MOUTH!' And then she seems surprised when suddenly she is unable to leave the court because she accepted the faeries beverages. She had one job, ONE JOB. DON'T FUCKING DRINK ANYTHING! My god, she's a burden to everyone! Honestly, if I had to drag that dip shit around I would have just left her at the court. I think the only thing I severely hated about this series was that we were forced to read within the eyes of Clary and her magical powers.<br /><br />And the other characters. A lot of people don't like Jace. I'm one of them. All he ever does throughout the series is sulk. He sulks more than a 5 year-old girl. Whenever something doesn't seem to be going Jace's way; he'll throw a tantrum and maybe punch a few windows. I have to admit though, he isn't the weakest character in the book and I did actually enjoy reading about him since he is funny and at least has a little more common sense than Clary.<br /><br />And of course we have the really good characters. I adored Magnus for a starter, by far one of the most beloved characters in the entire series. And Simon too, along with Alec (he improved as the books went on), Isabelle, and of course Sebastian. I hated Jocelyn. Worst mother ever. But I found Simon another fun to read as he had his flaws and his advantages, his entire character also wasn't built up around misery like Maia's was. Same with Magnus who also seems to just stand out by himself with his wacky behaviour. I found Alec interesting because he was one of was one of the only characters that held some kind of mystery to him. I loved how held back he was and how he progressed as the series went on. I also loved Isabelle for being the only true strong female character in the series. Cassandra tried to pass Clary off as this but honestly Clary has the emotional strength of an apple. Maia was just pathetic. But to me Isabelle really stood up well and I enjoyed reading about her.<br /><br />One of the things I liked about Cassandra's writing is her description. Like the Infernal Devices; she's always been great at describing characters and surroundings. I have noticed that all her characters just so happen to be outstandingly attractive but I do like the way she describes them in full detail instead of just throwing in the brief comment about their hair and maybe the colour of their eyes. I do think she overuses the eye colour description since any normal person really doesn't pay that much attention to someone's eyes... and also any normal person doesn't have eyes that miraculously change colour like Jace's do.<br /><br />I also liked Cassandra's way of grabbing your emotions. I mentioned this in the Infernal Devices review. I do think she does it a little better in The Infernal Devices; but that's probably just because The Infernal Devices was written a little later when she had probably got better at writing. But she still has this unique way of making you feel sad when she wants you to feel sad and making you feel happy when she wants you to feel happy. At times I even felt myself maybe sympathising with Clary or feeling rejoice for Clary even though I hate her guts and wanted her to maybe fall off a cliff or something (she certainly seems capable of doing that since she's the most useless character in the entire series)... well, you sympathised with the characters you were SUPPOSED to sympathise with anyway.<br /><br />because to be honest... the character I felt sorry for the most was Sebastian. The most tortured character in the entire series. I didn't care about Maia, I didn't care about Clary (aside from the frustration she felt with Jace), I sort of cared about Jace, and I didn't really care about Alec up until City Of Heavenly Fire. But the character I felt most sorry for was Sebastian. To be honest, I didn't BLAME him for being fucked up. And I partially blamed Jocelyn... in fact I REALLY blamed Jocelyn. Let's break it down shall we?<br /><br />- He was experimented on by his own father<br />- He was abandoned by his own mother. I don't care whether she thought a baby was 'evil' or not; abandoning a child like that is fucking disgraceful. Even if she thought he was dead; she could have maybe seemed a little bit happy to find her dead son actually alive. Remember, when Jocelyn discovered it in City of Glass she didn't really know about what he had done and just how evil he was. She knew about some things but she hadn't been there to witness it herself and the hate she had for him was mainly based around the idea of what she experienced when he was a baby. Which was just stupid. No wonder she gave up being a Shadowhunter if she was scared of a fucking baby.<br />-He was lonely. One of a kind. He was brought up with his only company being Valentine. But Valentine hated him and betrayed him. Then Sebastian found hope in Clary and thought she would be like him. But then found out that Clary hated him and was a dumbass. <br /><br />I mean, no one sympathised with him at all. Clary mentioned it for like a paragraph that maybe, just maybe, there was a reason for Sebastian being like this (she said it was loneliness). But no one tried to help him. No one even bothered to maybe make him understand he was wrong. Instead, Cassandra went on the 'KILL DA BAD GUY' routine that I'm kind of tired of. He was such an interesting character that could have brought on an interesting plot line but instead we had the average 'good guy' 'bad guy' routine of the flawless heroes tracking down the bad guy. I understand why Cassandra didn't kill him off. But I also hate the fact that Sebastian's character wasn't really appreciated enough because he really was the most interesting to read about. In the end he was just the psychopath with that one unexplainable and completely uninteresting motive of killing everybody for no apparent reason. I mean, he was supposed to be smart wasn't he? And he was also supposed to be lonely:<br /><br />Killing people doesn't = friends. It just equals even more loneliness. <br /><br />You know what would have been interesting? If after Sebastian died he became a demon... that would have been cool. I mean, he's got the demon blood so it would have been interesting if he went to hell but came back as a demon who occasionally went up into the human world from time to time. Like the demons described in the Downworlder bars or something.<br /><br />So there we have it. It was a very enjoyable series. The only problem (I didn't have this) that my friends have mentioned, is that it starts of REALLY slowly. I've tried to get several people to read this series and most of them couldn't get into it because the books are so big and in some parts they really do just drag out. I have to admit that I felt this when reading the first and second book. I just struggled to make my way through them. But by the time I got to the third I was hooked... and it was even better when I discovered that there were another two books to the series! Yeah... I didn't realise it was a (then) five book series and I was thrilled to find out that there were even more of them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7876183526680733279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3312272977" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3312272977" />
    <a title="Hades_Child13" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111178638-hades-child13"><img alt="Hades_Child13" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3312272977?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hades_Child13" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hades_Child13" href="/user/show/111178638-hades-child13">Hades_Child13</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3312272977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7081753218043529628">I wanted to like this series. I really did. It seemed like a good idea to read, since I'm into other Young Adult/Middle Grade series. So I cracked open the first book and forced myself through the rest of them.<br/><br/>The concept of this book was pretty good. When I first heard that it was based on Christianity, I thought, "Wow, it'll probably educate me like Rick Riordan's books do!" Now I laugh about how wrong I was. The characters being Nephilim was just an excuse to make them fight stuff, not a crea</span>
  <span id="freeText7081753218043529628" style="display:none">I wanted to like this series. I really did. It seemed like a good idea to read, since I'm into other Young Adult/Middle Grade series. So I cracked open the first book and forced myself through the rest of them.<br /><br />The concept of this book was pretty good. When I first heard that it was based on Christianity, I thought, "Wow, it'll probably educate me like Rick Riordan's books do!" Now I laugh about how wrong I was. The characters being Nephilim was just an excuse to make them fight stuff, not a creative and interesting way to explore the Bible. I understand that this book wasn't intended to be informative, but I'm still disappointed that I didn't learn one. Single. Thing.<br /><br />Second, it was too heavy on the similes and metaphors. I'm still not clear on what color rainwater is. Blue? Clear? Blue-green? And also, how can something taste green? I wasn't aware that colors have their own distinctive flavors.<br /><br />My main problem was with the characters.<br /><br />CLARY: Having this girl as a main character made me want to scratch my eyes out. Forgot strong heroine-- she conveniently passed out every time there was danger. She's whiny, dumb, and very annoying. I don't understand why Simon and Jace both fell head-over-heels in love with her, because she's not even slightly likable. And I hated how every other character fawned over how beautiful and petite she was, but she remained completely oblivious to her own angelic looks. (It would be refreshing to read about an ugly protagonist, for once.) And she got into so many love triangles that I wanted to throw up.<br /><br />JACE: Throughout the entire series, I wanted to scream, "We get that everything about Jace is golden!" Because the physical descriptions are so over the top and unnecessary. I know that he's supposed to be the bad boy who really has a heart of gold (well, an everything of gold, as Mrs. Clare not-so-subtly tells us), but I saw no evidence of a heart of gold. He was arrogant, selfish, and tried to get sympathy by acting all tragic. I just plain hated him.<br /><br />ISABELLE: She's a beautiful heart breaker. That's what I got from reading these six books. What else? Well, she uses a whip and likes fancy clothes. I hated her, moving on.<br /><br />ALEC: I'm the most disappointed in the way Alec was written. I mean, he had potential (unlike most of the characters). I liked him at first because of the whole "trying not to be noticed thing," but then he opened his mouth and basically declared himself a jerk. I thought he was going to be the series's quiet, modest character, but it turned out there was no such character. He was just... there. He didn't really do anything important.<br /><br />SIMON: Simon is my favorite character, but that's not saying much. He didn't like the Pandemonium, which I thought was a good character trait. But he spent the whole series pining after Clary and ended up, like Alec, being a waste of potential.<br /><br />MAGNUS: Goes back and forth between wanted to help and getting all grumpy because he's the Shadowhunter's "pet warlock." He was interesting to read about, but not likable.<br /><br />VALENTINE: *Cough, Voldemort, cough.*<br /><br />SEBASTIAN: Horrible villain, no depth.<br /><br />EVERYONE ELSE: Boring, boring, boring, dead, boring.<br /><br />I read books to make friends with the characters. None of these were "this-person-is-my-new-best-friend" material.<br /><br /><br />So there you have it. This book had potential, but it was wasted. Interesting setting/concept, terrible characters. I wouldn't recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7081753218043529628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
